[Eng.4]	But these things have I told you, that when the time shall come, ye may remember that I told you of them. And these things I said not unto you at the beginning, because I was with you.
[Eng.5]	But now I go my way to him that sent me; and none of you asketh me, Whither goest thou?
[Eng.6]	But because I have said these things unto you, sorrow hath filled your heart.
[Eng.7]	Nevertheless I tell you the truth; It is expedient for you that I go away: for if I go not away, the Comforter will not come unto you; but if I depart, I will send him unto you.
[Eng.8]	And when he is come, he will reprove the world of sin, and of righteousness, and of judgment:
[Eng.9]	Of sin, because they believe not on me;
[Eng.10]	Of righteousness, because I go to my Father, and ye see me no more;
[Eng.11]	Of judgment, because the prince of this world is judged.
[Eng.12]	I have yet many things to say unto you, but ye cannot bear them now.
[Eng.13]	Howbeit when he, the Spirit of truth, is come, he will guide you into all truth: for he shall not speak of himself; but whatsoever he shall hear, that shall he speak: and he will shew you things to come.
[Eng.14]	He shall glorify me: for he shall receive of mine, and shall shew it unto you.
[Eng.15]	All things that the Father hath are mine: therefore said I, that he shall take of mine, and shall shew it unto you.
[Eng.16]	A little while, and ye shall not see me: and again, a little while, and ye shall see me, because I go to the Father.
[Eng.17]	Then said some of his disciples among themselves, What is this that he saith unto us, A little while, and ye shall not see me: and again, a little while, and ye shall see me: and, Because I go to the Father?
[Eng.18]	They said therefore, What is this that he saith, A little while? we cannot tell what he saith.
[Eng.19]	Now Jesus knew that they were desirous to ask him, and said unto them, Do ye enquire among yourselves of that I said, A little while, and ye shall not see me: and again, a little while, and ye shall see me?
[Eng.20]	Verily, verily, I say unto you, That ye shall weep and lament, but the world shall rejoice: and ye shall be sorrowful, but your sorrow shall be turned into joy.
[Eng.21]	A woman when she is in travail hath sorrow, because her hour is come: but as soon as she is delivered of the child, she remembereth no more the anguish, for joy that a man is born into the world.
[Eng.22]	And ye now therefore have sorrow: but I will see you again, and your heart shall rejoice, and your joy no man taketh from you.
[Eng.23]	And in that day ye shall ask me nothing. Verily, verily, I say unto you, Whatsoever ye shall ask the Father in my name, he will give it you.
[Eng.24]	Hitherto have ye asked nothing in my name: ask, and ye shall receive, that your joy may be full.
[Eng.25]	These things have I spoken unto you in proverbs: but the time cometh, when I shall no more speak unto you in proverbs, but I shall shew you plainly of the Father.
[Eng.26]	At that day ye shall ask in my name: and I say not unto you, that I will pray the Father for you:
[Eng.27]	For the Father himself loveth you, because ye have loved me, and have believed that I came out from God.
[Eng.28]	I came forth from the Father, and am come into the world: again, I leave the world, and go to the Father.
[Eng.29]	His disciples said unto him, Lo, now speakest thou plainly, and speakest no proverb.
[Eng.30]	Now are we sure that thou knowest all things, and needest not that any man should ask thee: by this we believe that thou camest forth from God.
[Eng.31]	Jesus answered them, Do ye now believe?
[Eng.32]	Behold, the hour cometh, yea, is now come, that ye shall be scattered, every man to his own, and shall leave me alone: and yet I am not alone, because the Father is with me.
[Eng.33]	These things I have spoken unto you, that in me ye might have peace. In the world ye shall have tribulation: but be of good cheer; I have overcome the world.
[Eng.1]	These words spake Jesus, and lifted up his eyes to heaven, and said, Father, the hour is come; glorify thy Son, that thy Son also may glorify thee:
[Eng.2]	As thou hast given him power over all flesh, that he should give eternal life to as many as thou hast given him.
[Eng.3]	And this is life eternal, that they might know thee the only true God, and Jesus Christ, whom thou hast sent.
[Eng.4]	I have glorified thee on the earth: I have finished the work which thou gavest me to do.
[Eng.5]	And now, O Father, glorify thou me with thine own self with the glory which I had with thee before the world was.
[Eng.6]	I have manifested thy name unto the men which thou gavest me out of the world: thine they were, and thou gavest them me; and they have kept thy word.
[Eng.7]	Now they have known that all things whatsoever thou hast given me are of thee.
[Eng.8]	For I have given unto them the words which thou gavest me; and they have received them, and have known surely that I came out from thee, and they have believed that thou didst send me.
[Eng.9]	I pray for them: I pray not for the world, but for them which thou hast given me; for they are thine.
[Eng.10]	And all mine are thine, and thine are mine; and I am glorified in them.
[Eng.11]	And now I am no more in the world, but these are in the world, and I come to thee. Holy Father, keep through thine own name those whom thou hast given me, that they may be one, as we are.
[Eng.12]	While I was with them in the world, I kept them in thy name: those that thou gavest me I have kept, and none of them is lost, but the son of perdition; that the scripture might be fulfilled.
[Eng.13]	And now come I to thee; and these things I speak in the world, that they might have my joy fulfilled in themselves.
[Eng.14]	I have given them thy word; and the world hath hated them, because they are not of the world, even as I am not of the world.
[Eng.15]	I pray not that thou shouldest take them out of the world, but that thou shouldest keep them from the evil.
[Eng.16]	They are not of the world, even as I am not of the world.
[Eng.17]	Sanctify them through thy truth: thy word is truth.
[Eng.18]	As thou hast sent me into the world, even so have I also sent them into the world.
[Eng.19]	And for their sakes I sanctify myself, that they also might be sanctified through the truth.
[Eng.20]	Neither pray I for these alone, but for them also which shall believe on me through their word;
[Eng.21]	That they all may be one; as thou, Father, art in me, and I in thee, that they also may be one in us: that the world may believe that thou hast sent me.
[Eng.22]	And the glory which thou gavest me I have given them; that they may be one, even as we are one:
[Eng.23]	I in them, and thou in me, that they may be made perfect in one; and that the world may know that thou hast sent me, and hast loved them, as thou hast loved me.
[Eng.24]	Father, I will that they also, whom thou hast given me, be with me where I am; that they may behold my glory, which thou hast given me: for thou lovedst me before the foundation of the world.
[Eng.25]	O righteous Father, the world hath not known thee: but I have known thee, and these have known that thou hast sent me.
[Eng.26]	And I have declared unto them thy name, and will declare it: that the love wherewith thou hast loved me may be in them, and I in them.
[Eng.1]	When Jesus had spoken these words, he went forth with his disciples over the brook Cedron, where was a garden, into the which he entered, and his disciples.
[Eng.2]	And Judas also, which betrayed him, knew the place: for Jesus ofttimes resorted thither with his disciples.
[Eng.3]	Judas then, having received a band of men and officers from the chief priests and Pharisees, cometh thither with lanterns and torches and weapons.
[Eng.4]	Jesus therefore, knowing all things that should come upon him, went forth, and said unto them, Whom seek ye?
[Eng.5]	They answered him, Jesus of Nazareth. Jesus saith unto them, I am he. And Judas also, which betrayed him, stood with them.
[Eng.6]	As soon then as he had said unto them, I am he, they went backward, and fell to the ground.
[Eng.7]	Then asked he them again, Whom seek ye? And they said, Jesus of Nazareth.
[Eng.8]	Jesus answered, I have told you that I am he: if therefore ye seek me, let these go their way:
[Eng.9]	That the saying might be fulfilled, which he spake, Of them which thou gavest me have I lost none.
[Eng.10]	Then Simon Peter having a sword drew it, and smote the high priest's servant, and cut off his right ear. The servant's name was Malchus.
[Eng.11]	Then said Jesus unto Peter, Put up thy sword into the sheath: the cup which my Father hath given me, shall I not drink it?
[Eng.12]	Then the band and the captain and officers of the Jews took Jesus, and bound him,
[Eng.13]	And led him away to Annas first; for he was father in law to Caiaphas, which was the high priest that same year.
[Eng.14]	Now Caiaphas was he, which gave counsel to the Jews, that it was expedient that one man should die for the people.
[Eng.15]	And Simon Peter followed Jesus, and so did another disciple: that disciple was known unto the high priest, and went in with Jesus into the palace of the high priest.
[Eng.16]	But Peter stood at the door without. Then went out that other disciple, which was known unto the high priest, and spake unto her that kept the door, and brought in Peter.
[Eng.17]	Then saith the damsel that kept the door unto Peter, Art not thou also one of this man's disciples? He saith, I am not.
[Eng.18]	And the servants and officers stood there, who had made a fire of coals; for it was cold: and they warmed themselves: and Peter stood with them, and warmed himself.
[Eng.19]	The high priest then asked Jesus of his disciples, and of his doctrine.
[Eng.20]	Jesus answered him, I spake openly to the world; I ever taught in the synagogue, and in the temple, whither the Jews always resort; and in secret have I said nothing.
[Eng.21]	Why askest thou me? ask them which heard me, what I have said unto them: behold, they know what I said.
[Eng.22]	And when he had thus spoken, one of the officers which stood by struck Jesus with the palm of his hand, saying, Answerest thou the high priest so?
[Eng.23]	Jesus answered him, If I have spoken evil, bear witness of the evil: but if well, why smitest thou me?
[Eng.24]	Now Annas had sent him bound unto Caiaphas the high priest.
[Eng.25]	And Simon Peter stood and warmed himself. They said therefore unto him, Art not thou also one of his disciples? He denied it, and said, I am not.
[Eng.26]	One of the servants of the high priest, being his kinsman whose ear Peter cut off, saith, Did not I see thee in the garden with him?
[Eng.27]	Peter then denied again: and immediately the cock crew.
[Eng.28]	Then led they Jesus from Caiaphas unto the hall of judgment: and it was early; and they themselves went not into the judgment hall, lest they should be defiled; but that they might eat the passover.
[Eng.29]	Pilate then went out unto them, and said, What accusation bring ye against this man?
[Eng.30]	They answered and said unto him, If he were not a malefactor, we would not have delivered him up unto thee.
[Eng.31]	Then said Pilate unto them, Take ye him, and judge him according to your law. The Jews therefore said unto him, It is not lawful for us to put any man to death:
[Eng.32]	That the saying of Jesus might be fulfilled, which he spake, signifying what death he should die.
[Eng.33]	Then Pilate entered into the judgment hall again, and called Jesus, and said unto him, Art thou the King of the Jews?
[Eng.34]	Jesus answered him, Sayest thou this thing of thyself, or did others tell it thee of me?
[Eng.35]	Pilate answered, Am I a Jew? Thine own nation and the chief priests have delivered thee unto me: what hast thou done?
[Eng.36]	Jesus answered, My kingdom is not of this world: if my kingdom were of this world, then would my servants fight, that I should not be delivered to the Jews: but now is my kingdom not from hence.
[Eng.37]	Pilate therefore said unto him, Art thou a king then? Jesus answered, Thou sayest that I am a king. To this end was I born, and for this cause came I into the world, that I should bear witness unto the truth. Every one that is of the truth heareth my voice.
[Eng.38]	Pilate saith unto him, What is truth? And when he had said this, he went out again unto the Jews, and saith unto them, I find in him no fault at all.
[Eng.39]	But ye have a custom, that I should release unto you one at the passover: will ye therefore that I release unto you the King of the Jews?
[Eng.40]	Then cried they all again, saying, Not this man, but Barabbas. Now Barabbas was a robber.
[Eng.1]	Then Pilate therefore took Jesus, and scourged him.
[Eng.2]	And the soldiers platted a crown of thorns, and put it on his head, and they put on him a purple robe,
[Eng.3]	And said, Hail, King of the Jews! and they smote him with their hands.
[Eng.4]	Pilate therefore went forth again, and saith unto them, Behold, I bring him forth to you, that ye may know that I find no fault in him.
[Eng.5]	Then came Jesus forth, wearing the crown of thorns, and the purple robe. And Pilate saith unto them, Behold the man!
[Eng.6]	When the chief priests therefore and officers saw him, they cried out, saying, Crucify him, crucify him. Pilate saith unto them, Take ye him, and crucify him: for I find no fault in him.
[Eng.7]	The Jews answered him, We have a law, and by our law he ought to die, because he made himself the Son of God.
[Eng.8]	When Pilate therefore heard that saying, he was the more afraid;
[Eng.9]	And went again into the judgment hall, and saith unto Jesus, Whence art thou? But Jesus gave him no answer.
[Eng.10]	Then saith Pilate unto him, Speakest thou not unto me? knowest thou not that I have power to crucify thee, and have power to release thee?
[Eng.11]	Jesus answered, Thou couldest have no power at all against me, except it were given thee from above: therefore he that delivered me unto thee hath the greater sin.
[Eng.12]	And from thenceforth Pilate sought to release him: but the Jews cried out, saying, If thou let this man go, thou art not Caesar's friend: whosoever maketh himself a king speaketh against Caesar.
[Eng.13]	When Pilate therefore heard that saying, he brought Jesus forth, and sat down in the judgment seat in a place that is called the Pavement, but in the Hebrew, Gabbatha.
[Eng.14]	And it was the preparation of the passover, and about the sixth hour: and he saith unto the Jews, Behold your King!
[Eng.15]	But they cried out, Away with him, away with him, crucify him. Pilate saith unto them, Shall I crucify your King? The chief priests answered, We have no king but Caesar.
[Eng.16]	Then delivered he him therefore unto them to be crucified. And they took Jesus, and led him away.
[Eng.17]	And he bearing his cross went forth into a place called the place of a skull, which is called in the Hebrew Golgotha:
[Eng.18]	Where they crucified him, and two other with him, on either side one, and Jesus in the midst.
[Eng.19]	And Pilate wrote a title, and put it on the cross. And the writing was JESUS OF NAZARETH THE KING OF THE JEWS.
[Eng.20]	This title then read many of the Jews: for the place where Jesus was crucified was nigh to the city: and it was written in Hebrew, and Greek, and Latin.
[Eng.21]	Then said the chief priests of the Jews to Pilate, Write not, The King of the Jews; but that he said, I am King of the Jews.
[Eng.22]	Pilate answered, What I have written I have written.
[Eng.23]	Then the soldiers, when they had crucified Jesus, took his garments, and made four parts, to every soldier a part; and also his coat: now the coat was without seam, woven from the top throughout.
[Eng.24]	They said therefore among themselves, Let us not rend it, but cast lots for it, whose it shall be: that the scripture might be fulfilled, which saith, They parted my raiment among them, and for my vesture they did cast lots. These things therefore the soldiers did.
[Eng.25]	Now there stood by the cross of Jesus his mother, and his mother's sister, Mary the wife of Cleophas, and Mary Magdalene.
[Eng.26]	When Jesus therefore saw his mother, and the disciple standing by, whom he loved, he saith unto his mother, Woman, behold thy son!
[Eng.27]	Then saith he to the disciple, Behold thy mother! And from that hour that disciple took her unto his own home.
[Eng.28]	After this, Jesus knowing that all things were now accomplished, that the scripture might be fulfilled, saith, I thirst.
[Eng.29]	Now there was set a vessel full of vinegar: and they filled a spunge with vinegar, and put it upon hyssop, and put it to his mouth.
[Eng.30]	When Jesus therefore had received the vinegar, he said, It is finished: and he bowed his head, and gave up the ghost.
[Eng.31]	The Jews therefore, because it was the preparation, that the bodies should not remain upon the cross on the sabbath day, (for that sabbath day was an high day,) besought Pilate that their legs might be broken, and that they might be taken away.
[Eng.32]	Then came the soldiers, and brake the legs of the first, and of the other which was crucified with him.
[Eng.33]	But when they came to Jesus, and saw that he was dead already, they brake not his legs:
[Eng.34]	But one of the soldiers with a spear pierced his side, and forthwith came there out blood and water.
[Eng.35]	And he that saw it bare record, and his record is true: and he knoweth that he saith true, that ye might believe.
[Eng.36]	For these things were done, that the scripture should be fulfilled, A bone of him shall not be broken.
[Eng.37]	And again another scripture saith, They shall look on him whom they pierced.
[Eng.38]	And after this Joseph of Arimathaea, being a disciple of Jesus, but secretly for fear of the Jews, besought Pilate that he might take away the body of Jesus: and Pilate gave him leave. He came therefore, and took the body of Jesus.
[Eng.39]	And there came also Nicodemus, which at the first came to Jesus by night, and brought a mixture of myrrh and aloes, about an hundred pound weight.
[Eng.40]	Then took they the body of Jesus, and wound it in linen clothes with the spices, as the manner of the Jews is to bury.
[Eng.41]	Now in the place where he was crucified there was a garden; and in the garden a new sepulchre, wherein was never man yet laid.
[Eng.42]	There laid they Jesus therefore because of the Jews' preparation day; for the sepulchre was nigh at hand.
[Eng.1]	The first day of the week cometh Mary Magdalene early, when it was yet dark, unto the sepulchre, and seeth the stone taken away from the sepulchre.
[Eng.2]	Then she runneth, and cometh to Simon Peter, and to the other disciple, whom Jesus loved, and saith unto them, They have taken away the LORD out of the sepulchre, and we know not where they have laid him.
[Eng.3]	Peter therefore went forth, and that other disciple, and came to the sepulchre.
[Eng.4]	So they ran both together: and the other disciple did outrun Peter, and came first to the sepulchre.
[Eng.5]	And he stooping down, and looking in, saw the linen clothes lying; yet went he not in.
[Eng.6]	Then cometh Simon Peter following him, and went into the sepulchre, and seeth the linen clothes lie,
[Eng.7]	And the napkin, that was about his head, not lying with the linen clothes, but wrapped together in a place by itself.
[Eng.8]	Then went in also that other disciple, which came first to the sepulchre, and he saw, and believed.
[Eng.9]	For as yet they knew not the scripture, that he must rise again from the dead.
[Eng.10]	Then the disciples went away again unto their own home.
[Eng.11]	But Mary stood without at the sepulchre weeping: and as she wept, she stooped down, and looked into the sepulchre,
[Eng.12]	And seeth two angels in white sitting, the one at the head, and the other at the feet, where the body of Jesus had lain.
[Eng.13]	And they say unto her, Woman, why weepest thou? She saith unto them, Because they have taken away my LORD, and I know not where they have laid him.
[Eng.14]	And when she had thus said, she turned herself back, and saw Jesus standing, and knew not that it was Jesus.
[Eng.15]	Jesus saith unto her, Woman, why weepest thou? whom seekest thou? She, supposing him to be the gardener, saith unto him, Sir, if thou have borne him hence, tell me where thou hast laid him, and I will take him away.
[Eng.16]	Jesus saith unto her, Mary. She turned herself, and saith unto him, Rabboni; which is to say, Master.
[Eng.17]	Jesus saith unto her, Touch me not; for I am not yet ascended to my Father: but go to my brethren, and say unto them, I ascend unto my Father, and your Father; and to my God, and your God.
[Eng.18]	Mary Magdalene came and told the disciples that she had seen the LORD, and that he had spoken these things unto her.
[Eng.19]	Then the same day at evening, being the first day of the week, when the doors were shut where the disciples were assembled for fear of the Jews, came Jesus and stood in the midst, and saith unto them, Peace be unto you.
[Eng.20]	And when he had so said, he shewed unto them his hands and his side. Then were the disciples glad, when they saw the LORD.
[Eng.21]	Then said Jesus to them again, Peace be unto you: as my Father hath sent me, even so send I you.
[Eng.22]	And when he had said this, he breathed on them, and saith unto them, Receive ye the Holy Ghost:
[Eng.23]	Whose soever sins ye remit, they are remitted unto them; and whose soever sins ye retain, they are retained.
[Eng.24]	But Thomas, one of the twelve, called Didymus, was not with them when Jesus came.
[Eng.25]	The other disciples therefore said unto him, We have seen the LORD. But he said unto them, Except I shall see in his hands the print of the nails, and put my finger into the print of the nails, and thrust my hand into his side, I will not believe.
[Eng.26]	And after eight days again his disciples were within, and Thomas with them: then came Jesus, the doors being shut, and stood in the midst, and said, Peace be unto you.
[Eng.27]	Then saith he to Thomas, Reach hither thy finger, and behold my hands; and reach hither thy hand, and thrust it into my side: and be not faithless, but believing.
[Eng.28]	And Thomas answered and said unto him, My LORD and my God.
[Eng.29]	Jesus saith unto him, Thomas, because thou hast seen me, thou hast believed: blessed are they that have not seen, and yet have believed.
[Eng.30]	And many other signs truly did Jesus in the presence of his disciples, which are not written in this book:
[Eng.31]	But these are written, that ye might believe that Jesus is the Christ, the Son of God; and that believing ye might have life through his name.
[Eng.1]	After these things Jesus shewed himself again to the disciples at the sea of Tiberias; and on this wise shewed he himself.
[Eng.2]	There were together Simon Peter, and Thomas called Didymus, and Nathanael of Cana in Galilee, and the sons of Zebedee, and two other of his disciples.
[Eng.3]	Simon Peter saith unto them, I go a fishing. They say unto him, We also go with thee. They went forth, and entered into a ship immediately; and that night they caught nothing.
[Eng.4]	But when the morning was now come, Jesus stood on the shore: but the disciples knew not that it was Jesus.
[Eng.5]	Then Jesus saith unto them, Children, have ye any meat? They answered him, No.
[Eng.6]	And he said unto them, Cast the net on the right side of the ship, and ye shall find. They cast therefore, and now they were not able to draw it for the multitude of fishes.
[Eng.7]	Therefore that disciple whom Jesus loved saith unto Peter, It is the Lord. Now when Simon Peter heard that it was the Lord, he girt his fisher's coat unto him, (for he was naked,) and did cast himself into the sea.
[Eng.8]	And the other disciples came in a little ship; (for they were not far from land, but as it were two hundred cubits,) dragging the net with fishes.
[Eng.9]	As soon then as they were come to land, they saw a fire of coals there, and fish laid thereon, and bread.
[Eng.10]	Jesus saith unto them, Bring of the fish which ye have now caught.
[Eng.11]	Simon Peter went up, and drew the net to land full of great fishes, an hundred and fifty and three: and for all there were so many, yet was not the net broken.
[Eng.12]	Jesus saith unto them, Come and dine. And none of the disciples durst ask him, Who art thou? knowing that it was the Lord.
[Eng.13]	Jesus then cometh, and taketh bread, and giveth them, and fish likewise.
[Eng.14]	This is now the third time that Jesus shewed himself to his disciples, after that he was risen from the dead.
[Eng.15]	So when they had dined, Jesus saith to Simon Peter, Simon, son of Jonas, lovest thou me more than these? He saith unto him, Yea, Lord; thou knowest that I love thee. He saith unto him, Feed my lambs.
[Eng.16]	He saith to him again the second time, Simon, son of Jonas, lovest thou me? He saith unto him, Yea, Lord; thou knowest that I love thee. He saith unto him, Feed my sheep.
[Eng.17]	He saith unto him the third time, Simon, son of Jonas, lovest thou me? Peter was grieved because he said unto him the third time, Lovest thou me? And he said unto him, Lord, thou knowest all things; thou knowest that I love thee. Jesus saith unto him, Feed my sheep.
[Eng.18]	Verily, verily, I say unto thee, When thou wast young, thou girdest thyself, and walkedst whither thou wouldest: but when thou shalt be old, thou shalt stretch forth thy hands, and another shall gird thee, and carry thee whither thou wouldest not.
[Eng.19]	This spake he, signifying by what death he should glorify God. And when he had spoken this, he saith unto him, Follow me.
[Eng.20]	Then Peter, turning about, seeth the disciple whom Jesus loved following; which also leaned on his breast at supper, and said, Lord, which is he that betrayeth thee?
[Eng.21]	Peter seeing him saith to Jesus, Lord, and what shall this man do?
[Eng.22]	Jesus saith unto him, If I will that he tarry till I come, what is that to thee? follow thou me.
[Eng.23]	Then went this saying abroad among the brethren, that that disciple should not die: yet Jesus said not unto him, He shall not die; but, If I will that he tarry till I come, what is that to thee?
[Eng.24]	This is the disciple which testifieth of these things, and wrote these things: and we know that his testimony is true.
[Eng.25]	And there are also many other things which Jesus did, the which, if they should be written every one, I suppose that even the world itself could not contain the books that should be written. Amen.
[Eng.1]	The book of the generation of Jesus Christ, the son of David, the son of Abraham.
[Eng.2]	Abraham begat Isaac; and Isaac begat Jacob; and Jacob begat Judas and his brethren;
[Eng.3]	And Judas begat Phares and Zara of Thamar; and Phares begat Esrom; and Esrom begat Aram;
[Eng.4]	And Aram begat Aminadab; and Aminadab begat Naasson; and Naasson begat Salmon;
[Eng.5]	And Salmon begat Booz of Rachab; and Booz begat Obed of Ruth; and Obed begat Jesse;
[Eng.6]	And Jesse begat David the king; and David the king begat Solomon of her that had been the wife of Urias;
[Eng.7]	And Solomon begat Roboam; and Roboam begat Abia; and Abia begat Asa;
[Eng.8]	And Asa begat Josaphat; and Josaphat begat Joram; and Joram begat Ozias;
[Eng.9]	And Ozias begat Joatham; and Joatham begat Achaz; and Achaz begat Ezekias;
[Eng.10]	And Ezekias begat Manasses; and Manasses begat Amon; and Amon begat Josias;
[Eng.11]	And Josias begat Jechonias and his brethren, about the time they were carried away to Babylon:
[Eng.12]	And after they were brought to Babylon, Jechonias begat Salathiel; and Salathiel begat Zorobabel;
[Eng.13]	And Zorobabel begat Abiud; and Abiud begat Eliakim; and Eliakim begat Azor;
[Eng.14]	And Azor begat Sadoc; and Sadoc begat Achim; and Achim begat Eliud;
[Eng.15]	And Eliud begat Eleazar; and Eleazar begat Matthan; and Matthan begat Jacob;
[Eng.16]	And Jacob begat Joseph the husband of Mary, of whom was born Jesus, who is called Christ.
[Eng.17]	So all the generations from Abraham to David are fourteen generations; and from David until the carrying away into Babylon are fourteen generations; and from the carrying away into Babylon unto Christ are fourteen generations.
[Eng.18]	Now the birth of Jesus Christ was on this wise: When as his mother Mary was espoused to Joseph, before they came together, she was found with child of the Holy Ghost.
[Eng.19]	Then Joseph her husband, being a just man, and not willing to make her a publick example, was minded to put her away privily.
[Eng.20]	But while he thought on these things, behold, the angel of the LORD appeared unto him in a dream, saying, Joseph, thou son of David, fear not to take unto thee Mary thy wife: for that which is conceived in her is of the Holy Ghost.
[Eng.21]	And she shall bring forth a son, and thou shalt call his name JESUS: for he shall save his people from their sins.
[Eng.22]	Now all this was done, that it might be fulfilled which was spoken of the Lord by the prophet, saying,
[Eng.23]	Behold, a virgin shall be with child, and shall bring forth a son, and they shall call his name Emmanuel, which being interpreted is, God with us.
[Eng.24]	Then Joseph being raised from sleep did as the angel of the Lord had bidden him, and took unto him his wife:
[Eng.25]	And knew her not till she had brought forth her firstborn son: and he called his name JESUS.
[Eng.1]	Now when Jesus was born in Bethlehem of Judaea in the days of Herod the king, behold, there came wise men from the east to Jerusalem,
[Eng.2]	Saying, Where is he that is born King of the Jews? for we have seen his star in the east, and are come to worship him.
[Eng.3]	When Herod the king had heard these things, he was troubled, and all Jerusalem with him.
[Eng.4]	And when he had gathered all the chief priests and scribes of the people together, he demanded of them where Christ should be born.
[Eng.5]	And they said unto him, In Bethlehem of Judaea: for thus it is written by the prophet,
[Eng.6]	And thou Bethlehem, in the land of Juda, art not the least among the princes of Juda: for out of thee shall come a Governor, that shall rule my people Israel.
[Eng.7]	Then Herod, when he had privily called the wise men, enquired of them diligently what time the star appeared.
[Eng.8]	And he sent them to Bethlehem, and said, Go and search diligently for the young child; and when ye have found him, bring me word again, that I may come and worship him also.
[Eng.9]	When they had heard the king, they departed; and, lo, the star, which they saw in the east, went before them, till it came and stood over where the young child was.
[Eng.10]	When they saw the star, they rejoiced with exceeding great joy.
[Eng.11]	And when they were come into the house, they saw the young child with Mary his mother, and fell down, and worshipped him: and when they had opened their treasures, they presented unto him gifts; gold, and frankincense and myrrh.
[Eng.12]	And being warned of God in a dream that they should not return to Herod, they departed into their own country another way.
[Eng.13]	And when they were departed, behold, the angel of the Lord appeareth to Joseph in a dream, saying, Arise, and take the young child and his mother, and flee into Egypt, and be thou there until I bring thee word: for Herod will seek the young child to destroy him.
[Eng.14]	When he arose, he took the young child and his mother by night, and departed into Egypt:
[Eng.15]	And was there until the death of Herod: that it might be fulfilled which was spoken of the Lord by the prophet, saying, Out of Egypt have I called my son.
[Eng.16]	Then Herod, when he saw that he was mocked of the wise men, was exceeding wroth, and sent forth, and slew all the children that were in Bethlehem, and in all the coasts thereof, from two years old and under, according to the time which he had diligently enquired of the wise men.
[Eng.17]	Then was fulfilled that which was spoken by Jeremy the prophet, saying,
[Eng.18]	In Rama was there a voice heard, lamentation, and weeping, and great mourning, Rachel weeping for her children, and would not be comforted, because they are not.
[Eng.19]	But when Herod was dead, behold, an angel of the Lord appeareth in a dream to Joseph in Egypt,
[Eng.20]	Saying, Arise, and take the young child and his mother, and go into the land of Israel: for they are dead which sought the young child's life.
[Eng.21]	And he arose, and took the young child and his mother, and came into the land of Israel.
[Eng.22]	But when he heard that Archelaus did reign in Judaea in the room of his father Herod, he was afraid to go thither: notwithstanding, being warned of God in a dream, he turned aside into the parts of Galilee:
[Eng.23]	And he came and dwelt in a city called Nazareth: that it might be fulfilled which was spoken by the prophets, He shall be called a Nazarene.
[Eng.1]	In those days came John the Baptist, preaching in the wilderness of Judaea,
[Eng.2]	And saying, Repent ye: for the kingdom of heaven is at hand.
[Eng.3]	For this is he that was spoken of by the prophet Esaias, saying, The voice of one crying in the wilderness, Prepare ye the way of the Lord, make his paths straight.
[Eng.4]	And the same John had his raiment of camel's hair, and a leathern girdle about his loins; and his meat was locusts and wild honey.
[Eng.5]	Then went out to him Jerusalem, and all Judaea, and all the region round about Jordan,
[Eng.6]	And were baptized of him in Jordan, confessing their sins.
[Eng.7]	But when he saw many of the Pharisees and Sadducees come to his baptism, he said unto them, O generation of vipers, who hath warned you to flee from the wrath to come?
[Eng.8]	Bring forth therefore fruits meet for repentance:
[Eng.9]	And think not to say within yourselves, We have Abraham to our father: for I say unto you, that God is able of these stones to raise up children unto Abraham.
[Eng.10]	And now also the axe is laid unto the root of the trees: therefore every tree which bringeth not forth good fruit is hewn down, and cast into the fire.
[Eng.11]	I indeed baptize you with water unto repentance: but he that cometh after me is mightier than I, whose shoes I am not worthy to bear: he shall baptize you with the Holy Ghost, and with fire:
[Eng.12]	Whose fan is in his hand, and he will throughly purge his floor, and gather his wheat into the garner; but he will burn up the chaff with unquenchable fire.
[Eng.13]	Then cometh Jesus from Galilee to Jordan unto John, to be baptized of him.
[Eng.14]	But John forbad him, saying, I have need to be baptized of thee, and comest thou to me?
[Eng.15]	And Jesus answering said unto him, Suffer it to be so now: for thus it becometh us to fulfil all righteousness. Then he suffered him.
[Eng.16]	And Jesus, when he was baptized, went up straightway out of the water: and, lo, the heavens were opened unto him, and he saw the Spirit of God descending like a dove, and lighting upon him:
[Eng.17]	And lo a voice from heaven, saying, This is my beloved Son, in whom I am well pleased.
[Eng.1]	Then was Jesus led up of the spirit into the wilderness to be tempted of the devil.
[Eng.2]	And when he had fasted forty days and forty nights, he was afterward an hungred.
[Eng.3]	And when the tempter came to him, he said, If thou be the Son of God, command that these stones be made bread.
[Eng.4]	But he answered and said, It is written, Man shall not live by bread alone, but by every word that proceedeth out of the mouth of God.
[Eng.5]	Then the devil taketh him up into the holy city, and setteth him on a pinnacle of the temple,
[Eng.6]	And saith unto him, If thou be the Son of God, cast thyself down: for it is written, He shall give his angels charge concerning thee: and in their hands they shall bear thee up, lest at any time thou dash thy foot against a stone.
[Eng.7]	Jesus said unto him, It is written again, Thou shalt not tempt the Lord thy God.
[Eng.8]	Again, the devil taketh him up into an exceeding high mountain, and sheweth him all the kingdoms of the world, and the glory of them;
[Eng.9]	And saith unto him, All these things will I give thee, if thou wilt fall down and worship me.
[Eng.10]	Then saith Jesus unto him, Get thee hence, Satan: for it is written, Thou shalt worship the Lord thy God, and him only shalt thou serve.
[Eng.11]	Then the devil leaveth him, and, behold, angels came and ministered unto him.
[Eng.12]	Now when Jesus had heard that John was cast into prison, he departed into Galilee;
[Eng.13]	And leaving Nazareth, he came and dwelt in Capernaum, which is upon the sea coast, in the borders of Zabulon and Nephthalim:
[Eng.14]	That it might be fulfilled which was spoken by Esaias the prophet, saying,
[Eng.15]	The land of Zabulon, and the land of Nephthalim, by the way of the sea, beyond Jordan, Galilee of the Gentiles;
[Eng.16]	The people which sat in darkness saw great light; and to them which sat in the region and shadow of death light is sprung up.
[Eng.17]	From that time Jesus began to preach, and to say, Repent: for the kingdom of heaven is at hand.
[Eng.18]	And Jesus, walking by the sea of Galilee, saw two brethren, Simon called Peter, and Andrew his brother, casting a net into the sea: for they were fishers.
[Eng.19]	And he saith unto them, Follow me, and I will make you fishers of men.
[Eng.20]	And they straightway left their nets, and followed him.
[Eng.21]	And going on from thence, he saw other two brethren, James the son of Zebedee, and John his brother, in a ship with Zebedee their father, mending their nets; and he called them.
[Eng.22]	And they immediately left the ship and their father, and followed him.
[Eng.23]	And Jesus went about all Galilee, teaching in their synagogues, and preaching the gospel of the kingdom, and healing all manner of sickness and all manner of disease among the people.
[Eng.24]	And his fame went throughout all Syria: and they brought unto him all sick people that were taken with divers diseases and torments, and those which were possessed with devils, and those which were lunatick, and those that had the palsy; and he healed them.
[Eng.25]	And there followed him great multitudes of people from Galilee, and from Decapolis, and from Jerusalem, and from Judaea, and from beyond Jordan.
[Eng.1]	And seeing the multitudes, he went up into a mountain: and when he was set, his disciples came unto him:
[Eng.2]	And he opened his mouth, and taught them, saying,
[Eng.3]	Blessed are the poor in spirit: for theirs is the kingdom of heaven.
[Eng.4]	Blessed are they that mourn: for they shall be comforted.
[Eng.5]	Blessed are the meek: for they shall inherit the earth.
[Eng.6]	Blessed are they which do hunger and thirst after righteousness: for they shall be filled.
[Eng.7]	Blessed are the merciful: for they shall obtain mercy.
[Eng.8]	Blessed are the pure in heart: for they shall see God.
[Eng.9]	Blessed are the peacemakers: for they shall be called the children of God.
[Eng.10]	Blessed are they which are persecuted for righteousness' sake: for theirs is the kingdom of heaven.
[Eng.11]	Blessed are ye, when men shall revile you, and persecute you, and shall say all manner of evil against you falsely, for my sake.
[Eng.12]	Rejoice, and be exceeding glad: for great is your reward in heaven: for so persecuted they the prophets which were before you.
[Eng.13]	Ye are the salt of the earth: but if the salt have lost his savour, wherewith shall it be salted? it is thenceforth good for nothing, but to be cast out, and to be trodden under foot of men.
[Eng.14]	Ye are the light of the world. A city that is set on an hill cannot be hid.
[Eng.15]	Neither do men light a candle, and put it under a bushel, but on a candlestick; and it giveth light unto all that are in the house.
[Eng.16]	Let your light so shine before men, that they may see your good works, and glorify your Father which is in heaven.
[Eng.17]	Think not that I am come to destroy the law, or the prophets: I am not come to destroy, but to fulfil.
[Eng.18]	For verily I say unto you, Till heaven and earth pass, one jot or one tittle shall in no wise pass from the law, till all be fulfilled.
[Eng.19]	Whosoever therefore shall break one of these least commandments, and shall teach men so, he shall be called the least in the kingdom of heaven: but whosoever shall do and teach them, the same shall be called great in the kingdom of heaven.
[Eng.20]	For I say unto you, That except your righteousness shall exceed the righteousness of the scribes and Pharisees, ye shall in no case enter into the kingdom of heaven.
[Eng.21]	Ye have heard that it was said of them of old time, Thou shalt not kill; and whosoever shall kill shall be in danger of the judgment:
[Eng.22]	But I say unto you, That whosoever is angry with his brother without a cause shall be in danger of the judgment: and whosoever shall say to his brother, Raca, shall be in danger of the council: but whosoever shall say, Thou fool, shall be in danger of hell fire.
[Eng.23]	Therefore if thou bring thy gift to the altar, and there rememberest that thy brother hath ought against thee;
[Eng.24]	Leave there thy gift before the altar, and go thy way; first be reconciled to thy brother, and then come and offer thy gift.
[Eng.25]	Agree with thine adversary quickly, whiles thou art in the way with him; lest at any time the adversary deliver thee to the judge, and the judge deliver thee to the officer, and thou be cast into prison.
[Eng.26]	Verily I say unto thee, Thou shalt by no means come out thence, till thou hast paid the uttermost farthing.
[Eng.27]	Ye have heard that it was said by them of old time, Thou shalt not commit adultery:
[Eng.28]	But I say unto you, That whosoever looketh on a woman to lust after her hath committed adultery with her already in his heart.
[Eng.29]	And if thy right eye offend thee, pluck it out, and cast it from thee: for it is profitable for thee that one of thy members should perish, and not that thy whole body should be cast into hell.
[Eng.30]	And if thy right hand offend thee, cut it off, and cast it from thee: for it is profitable for thee that one of thy members should perish, and not that thy whole body should be cast into hell.
[Eng.31]	It hath been said, Whosoever shall put away his wife, let him give her a writing of divorcement:
[Eng.32]	But I say unto you, That whosoever shall put away his wife, saving for the cause of fornication, causeth her to commit adultery: and whosoever shall marry her that is divorced committeth adultery.
[Eng.33]	Again, ye have heard that it hath been said by them of old time, Thou shalt not forswear thyself, but shalt perform unto the Lord thine oaths:
[Eng.34]	But I say unto you, Swear not at all; neither by heaven; for it is God's throne:
[Eng.35]	Nor by the earth; for it is his footstool: neither by Jerusalem; for it is the city of the great King.
[Eng.36]	Neither shalt thou swear by thy head, because thou canst not make one hair white or black.
[Eng.37]	But let your communication be, Yea, yea; Nay, nay: for whatsoever is more than these cometh of evil.
[Eng.38]	Ye have heard that it hath been said, An eye for an eye, and a tooth for a tooth:
[Eng.39]	But I say unto you, That ye resist not evil: but whosoever shall smite thee on thy right cheek, turn to him the other also.
[Eng.40]	And if any man will sue thee at the law, and take away thy coat, let him have thy cloak also.
[Eng.41]	And whosoever shall compel thee to go a mile, go with him twain.
[Eng.42]	Give to him that asketh thee, and from him that would borrow of thee turn not thou away.
[Eng.43]	Ye have heard that it hath been said, Thou shalt love thy neighbour, and hate thine enemy.
[Eng.44]	But I say unto you, Love your enemies, bless them that curse you, do good to them that hate you, and pray for them which despitefully use you, and persecute you;
[Eng.45]	That ye may be the children of your Father which is in heaven: for he maketh his sun to rise on the evil and on the good, and sendeth rain on the just and on the unjust.
[Eng.46]	For if ye love them which love you, what reward have ye? do not even the publicans the same?
[Eng.47]	And if ye salute your brethren only, what do ye more than others? do not even the publicans so?
[Eng.48]	Be ye therefore perfect, even as your Father which is in heaven is perfect.
[Eng.1]	Take heed that ye do not your alms before men, to be seen of them: otherwise ye have no reward of your Father which is in heaven.
[Eng.2]	Therefore when thou doest thine alms, do not sound a trumpet before thee, as the hypocrites do in the synagogues and in the streets, that they may have glory of men. Verily I say unto you, They have their reward.
[Eng.3]	But when thou doest alms, let not thy left hand know what thy right hand doeth:
[Eng.4]	That thine alms may be in secret: and thy Father which seeth in secret himself shall reward thee openly.
[Eng.5]	And when thou prayest, thou shalt not be as the hypocrites are: for they love to pray standing in the synagogues and in the corners of the streets, that they may be seen of men. Verily I say unto you, They have their reward.
[Eng.6]	But thou, when thou prayest, enter into thy closet, and when thou hast shut thy door, pray to thy Father which is in secret; and thy Father which seeth in secret shall reward thee openly.
[Eng.7]	But when ye pray, use not vain repetitions, as the heathen do: for they think that they shall be heard for their much speaking.
[Eng.8]	Be not ye therefore like unto them: for your Father knoweth what things ye have need of, before ye ask him.
[Eng.9]	After this manner therefore pray ye: Our Father which art in heaven, Hallowed be thy name.
[Eng.10]	Thy kingdom come, Thy will be done in earth, as it is in heaven.
[Eng.11]	Give us this day our daily bread.
[Eng.12]	And forgive us our debts, as we forgive our debtors.
[Eng.13]	And lead us not into temptation, but deliver us from evil: For thine is the kingdom, and the power, and the glory, for ever. Amen.
[Eng.14]	For if ye forgive men their trespasses, your heavenly Father will also forgive you:
[Eng.15]	But if ye forgive not men their trespasses, neither will your Father forgive your trespasses.
[Eng.16]	Moreover when ye fast, be not, as the hypocrites, of a sad countenance: for they disfigure their faces, that they may appear unto men to fast. Verily I say unto you, They have their reward.
[Eng.17]	But thou, when thou fastest, anoint thine head, and wash thy face;
[Eng.18]	That thou appear not unto men to fast, but unto thy Father which is in secret: and thy Father, which seeth in secret, shall reward thee openly.
[Eng.19]	Lay not up for yourselves treasures upon earth, where moth and rust doth corrupt, and where thieves break through and steal:
[Eng.20]	But lay up for yourselves treasures in heaven, where neither moth nor rust doth corrupt, and where thieves do not break through nor steal:
[Eng.21]	For where your treasure is, there will your heart be also.
[Eng.22]	The light of the body is the eye: if therefore thine eye be single, thy whole body shall be full of light.
[Eng.23]	But if thine eye be evil, thy whole body shall be full of darkness. If therefore the light that is in thee be darkness, how great is that darkness!
[Eng.24]	No man can serve two masters: for either he will hate the one, and love the other; or else he will hold to the one, and despise the other. Ye cannot serve God and mammon.
[Eng.25]	Therefore I say unto you, Take no thought for your life, what ye shall eat, or what ye shall drink; nor yet for your body, what ye shall put on. Is not the life more than meat, and the body than raiment?
[Eng.26]	Behold the fowls of the air: for they sow not, neither do they reap, nor gather into barns; yet your heavenly Father feedeth them. Are ye not much better than they?
[Eng.27]	Which of you by taking thought can add one cubit unto his stature?
[Eng.28]	And why take ye thought for raiment? Consider the lilies of the field, how they grow; they toil not, neither do they spin:
[Eng.29]	And yet I say unto you, That even Solomon in all his glory was not arrayed like one of these.
[Eng.30]	Wherefore, if God so clothe the grass of the field, which to day is, and to morrow is cast into the oven, shall he not much more clothe you, O ye of little faith?
[Eng.31]	Therefore take no thought, saying, What shall we eat? or, What shall we drink? or, Wherewithal shall we be clothed?
[Eng.32]	(For after all these things do the Gentiles seek:) for your heavenly Father knoweth that ye have need of all these things.
[Eng.33]	But seek ye first the kingdom of God, and his righteousness; and all these things shall be added unto you.
[Eng.34]	Take therefore no thought for the morrow: for the morrow shall take thought for the things of itself. Sufficient unto the day is the evil thereof.
[Eng.1]	Judge not, that ye be not judged.
[Eng.2]	For with what judgment ye judge, ye shall be judged: and with what measure ye mete, it shall be measured to you again.
[Eng.3]	And why beholdest thou the mote that is in thy brother's eye, but considerest not the beam that is in thine own eye?
[Eng.4]	Or how wilt thou say to thy brother, Let me pull out the mote out of thine eye; and, behold, a beam is in thine own eye?
[Eng.5]	Thou hypocrite, first cast out the beam out of thine own eye; and then shalt thou see clearly to cast out the mote out of thy brother's eye.
[Eng.6]	Give not that which is holy unto the dogs, neither cast ye your pearls before swine, lest they trample them under their feet, and turn again and rend you.
[Eng.7]	Ask, and it shall be given you; seek, and ye shall find; knock, and it shall be opened unto you:
[Eng.8]	For every one that asketh receiveth; and he that seeketh findeth; and to him that knocketh it shall be opened.
[Eng.9]	Or what man is there of you, whom if his son ask bread, will he give him a stone?
[Eng.10]	Or if he ask a fish, will he give him a serpent?
[Eng.11]	If ye then, being evil, know how to give good gifts unto your children, how much more shall your Father which is in heaven give good things to them that ask him?
[Eng.12]	Therefore all things whatsoever ye would that men should do to you, do ye even so to them: for this is the law and the prophets.
[Eng.13]	Enter ye in at the strait gate: for wide is the gate, and broad is the way, that leadeth to destruction, and many there be which go in thereat:
[Eng.14]	Because strait is the gate, and narrow is the way, which leadeth unto life, and few there be that find it.
[Eng.15]	Beware of false prophets, which come to you in sheep's clothing, but inwardly they are ravening wolves.
[Eng.16]	Ye shall know them by their fruits. Do men gather grapes of thorns, or figs of thistles?
[Eng.17]	Even so every good tree bringeth forth good fruit; but a corrupt tree bringeth forth evil fruit.
[Eng.18]	A good tree cannot bring forth evil fruit, neither can a corrupt tree bring forth good fruit.
[Eng.19]	Every tree that bringeth not forth good fruit is hewn down, and cast into the fire.
[Eng.20]	Wherefore by their fruits ye shall know them.
[Eng.21]	Not every one that saith unto me, Lord, Lord, shall enter into the kingdom of heaven; but he that doeth the will of my Father which is in heaven.
[Eng.22]	Many will say to me in that day, Lord, Lord, have we not prophesied in thy name? and in thy name have cast out devils? and in thy name done many wonderful works?
[Eng.23]	And then will I profess unto them, I never knew you: depart from me, ye that work iniquity.
[Eng.24]	Therefore whosoever heareth these sayings of mine, and doeth them, I will liken him unto a wise man, which built his house upon a rock:
[Eng.25]	And the rain descended, and the floods came, and the winds blew, and beat upon that house; and it fell not: for it was founded upon a rock.
[Eng.26]	And every one that heareth these sayings of mine, and doeth them not, shall be likened unto a foolish man, which built his house upon the sand:
[Eng.27]	And the rain descended, and the floods came, and the winds blew, and beat upon that house; and it fell: and great was the fall of it.
[Eng.28]	And it came to pass, when Jesus had ended these sayings, the people were astonished at his doctrine:
[Eng.29]	For he taught them as one having authority, and not as the scribes.

Ikkeri is situated in Sagara taluk about 6km to the south of Sagara. The word Ikkeri in Kannada means "Two Streets".
Nandi mantap
Gallery
Aghoresvara temple
Nayakas of Ikkeri
Vijay Rupani is an Indian politician from the Bharatiya Janata Party. He is an incumbent Chief Minister of Gujarat, a western state in India, since 7 August 2016 and a member of the Gujarat Legislative Assembly representing Rajkot West and presently the state president of the party.
Career
On 19 February 2016, Rupani became the state BJP president, replacing R. C. Faldu. In August 2014, when Vajubhai Vala, the incumbent speaker of Gujarat Legislative Assembly, resigned as the MLA from Rajkot West as he was appointed as the governor of Karnataka. Vijay Rupani was nominated by the BJP to contest his vacant seat.
He won the bypoll on 19 October 2014 by a huge margin.
I am not the mind, the intellect, the ego or the memory, I am not the ears, the skin, the nose or the eyes, I am not space, not earth, not fire, water or wind,
I am not the breath, nor the five elements, I am not matter, nor the 5 sheaths of conciousness Nor am I the speech, the hands, or the feet,
There is no like or dislike in me, no greed or delusion, I know not pride or jealousy, I have no duty, no desire for wealth, lust or liberation,
No virtue or vice, no pleasure or pain, I need no mantras, no pilgrimage, no scriptures or rituals, I am not the experienced, nor the experience itself,

[Eng.1]	When he was come down from the mountain, great multitudes followed him.
[Eng.2]	And, behold, there came a leper and worshipped him, saying, Lord, if thou wilt, thou canst make me clean.
[Eng.3]	And Jesus put forth his hand, and touched him, saying, I will; be thou clean. And immediately his leprosy was cleansed.
[Eng.4]	And Jesus saith unto him, See thou tell no man; but go thy way, shew thyself to the priest, and offer the gift that Moses commanded, for a testimony unto them.
[Eng.5]	And when Jesus was entered into Capernaum, there came unto him a centurion, beseeching him,
[Eng.6]	And saying, Lord, my servant lieth at home sick of the palsy, grievously tormented.
[Eng.7]	And Jesus saith unto him, I will come and heal him.
[Eng.8]	The centurion answered and said, Lord, I am not worthy that thou shouldest come under my roof: but speak the word only, and my servant shall be healed.
[Eng.9]	For I am a man under authority, having soldiers under me: and I say to this man, Go, and he goeth; and to another, Come, and he cometh; and to my servant, Do this, and he doeth it.
[Eng.10]	When Jesus heard it, he marvelled, and said to them that followed, Verily I say unto you, I have not found so great faith, no, not in Israel.
[Eng.11]	And I say unto you, That many shall come from the east and west, and shall sit down with Abraham, and Isaac, and Jacob, in the kingdom of heaven.
[Eng.12]	But the children of the kingdom shall be cast out into outer darkness: there shall be weeping and gnashing of teeth.
[Eng.13]	And Jesus said unto the centurion, Go thy way; and as thou hast believed, so be it done unto thee. And his servant was healed in the selfsame hour.
[Eng.14]	And when Jesus was come into Peter's house, he saw his wife's mother laid, and sick of a fever.
[Eng.15]	And he touched her hand, and the fever left her: and she arose, and ministered unto them.
[Eng.16]	When the even was come, they brought unto him many that were possessed with devils: and he cast out the spirits with his word, and healed all that were sick:
[Eng.17]	That it might be fulfilled which was spoken by Esaias the prophet, saying, Himself took our infirmities, and bare our sicknesses.
[Eng.18]	Now when Jesus saw great multitudes about him, he gave commandment to depart unto the other side.
[Eng.19]	And a certain scribe came, and said unto him, Master, I will follow thee whithersoever thou goest.
[Eng.20]	And Jesus saith unto him, The foxes have holes, and the birds of the air have nests; but the Son of man hath not where to lay his head.
[Eng.21]	And another of his disciples said unto him, Lord, suffer me first to go and bury my father.
[Eng.22]	But Jesus said unto him, Follow me; and let the dead bury their dead.
[Eng.23]	And when he was entered into a ship, his disciples followed him.
[Eng.24]	And, behold, there arose a great tempest in the sea, insomuch that the ship was covered with the waves: but he was asleep.
[Eng.25]	And his disciples came to him, and awoke him, saying, Lord, save us: we perish.
[Eng.26]	And he saith unto them, Why are ye fearful, O ye of little faith? Then he arose, and rebuked the winds and the sea; and there was a great calm.
[Eng.27]	But the men marvelled, saying, What manner of man is this, that even the winds and the sea obey him!
[Eng.28]	And when he was come to the other side into the country of the Gergesenes, there met him two possessed with devils, coming out of the tombs, exceeding fierce, so that no man might pass by that way.
[Eng.29]	And, behold, they cried out, saying, What have we to do with thee, Jesus, thou Son of God? art thou come hither to torment us before the time?
[Eng.30]	And there was a good way off from them an herd of many swine feeding.
[Eng.31]	So the devils besought him, saying, If thou cast us out, suffer us to go away into the herd of swine.
[Eng.32]	And he said unto them, Go. And when they were come out, they went into the herd of swine: and, behold, the whole herd of swine ran violently down a steep place into the sea, and perished in the waters.
[Eng.33]	And they that kept them fled, and went their ways into the city, and told every thing, and what was befallen to the possessed of the devils.
[Eng.34]	And, behold, the whole city came out to meet Jesus: and when they saw him, they besought him that he would depart out of their coasts.
[Eng.1]	And he entered into a ship, and passed over, and came into his own city.
[Eng.2]	And, behold, they brought to him a man sick of the palsy, lying on a bed: and Jesus seeing their faith said unto the sick of the palsy; Son, be of good cheer; thy sins be forgiven thee.
[Eng.3]	And, behold, certain of the scribes said within themselves, This man blasphemeth.
[Eng.4]	And Jesus knowing their thoughts said, Wherefore think ye evil in your hearts?
[Eng.5]	For whether is easier, to say, Thy sins be forgiven thee; or to say, Arise, and walk?
[Eng.6]	But that ye may know that the Son of man hath power on earth to forgive sins, (then saith he to the sick of the palsy,) Arise, take up thy bed, and go unto thine house.
[Eng.7]	And he arose, and departed to his house.
[Eng.8]	But when the multitudes saw it, they marvelled, and glorified God, which had given such power unto men.
[Eng.9]	And as Jesus passed forth from thence, he saw a man, named Matthew, sitting at the receipt of custom: and he saith unto him, Follow me. And he arose, and followed him.
[Eng.10]	And it came to pass, as Jesus sat at meat in the house, behold, many publicans and sinners came and sat down with him and his disciples.
[Eng.11]	And when the Pharisees saw it, they said unto his disciples, Why eateth your Master with publicans and sinners?
[Eng.12]	But when Jesus heard that, he said unto them, They that be whole need not a physician, but they that are sick.
[Eng.13]	But go ye and learn what that meaneth, I will have mercy, and not sacrifice: for I am not come to call the righteous, but sinners to repentance.
[Eng.14]	Then came to him the disciples of John, saying, Why do we and the Pharisees fast oft, but thy disciples fast not?
[Eng.15]	And Jesus said unto them, Can the children of the bridechamber mourn, as long as the bridegroom is with them? but the days will come, when the bridegroom shall be taken from them, and then shall they fast.
[Eng.16]	No man putteth a piece of new cloth unto an old garment, for that which is put in to fill it up taketh from the garment, and the rent is made worse.
[Eng.17]	Neither do men put new wine into old bottles: else the bottles break, and the wine runneth out, and the bottles perish: but they put new wine into new bottles, and both are preserved.
[Eng.18]	While he spake these things unto them, behold, there came a certain ruler, and worshipped him, saying, My daughter is even now dead: but come and lay thy hand upon her, and she shall live.
[Eng.19]	And Jesus arose, and followed him, and so did his disciples.
[Eng.20]	And, behold, a woman, which was diseased with an issue of blood twelve years, came behind him, and touched the hem of his garment:
[Eng.21]	For she said within herself, If I may but touch his garment, I shall be whole.
[Eng.22]	But Jesus turned him about, and when he saw her, he said, Daughter, be of good comfort; thy faith hath made thee whole. And the woman was made whole from that hour.
[Eng.23]	And when Jesus came into the ruler's house, and saw the minstrels and the people making a noise,
[Eng.24]	He said unto them, Give place: for the maid is not dead, but sleepeth. And they laughed him to scorn.
[Eng.25]	But when the people were put forth, he went in, and took her by the hand, and the maid arose.
[Eng.26]	And the fame hereof went abroad into all that land.
[Eng.27]	And when Jesus departed thence, two blind men followed him, crying, and saying, Thou son of David, have mercy on us.
[Eng.28]	And when he was come into the house, the blind men came to him: and Jesus saith unto them, Believe ye that I am able to do this? They said unto him, Yea, Lord.
[Eng.29]	Then touched he their eyes, saying, According to your faith be it unto you.
[Eng.30]	And their eyes were opened; and Jesus straitly charged them, saying, See that no man know it.
[Eng.31]	But they, when they were departed, spread abroad his fame in all that country.
[Eng.32]	As they went out, behold, they brought to him a dumb man possessed with a devil.
[Eng.33]	And when the devil was cast out, the dumb spake: and the multitudes marvelled, saying, It was never so seen in Israel.
[Eng.34]	But the Pharisees said, He casteth out devils through the prince of the devils.
[Eng.35]	And Jesus went about all the cities and villages, teaching in their synagogues, and preaching the gospel of the kingdom, and healing every sickness and every disease among the people.
[Eng.36]	But when he saw the multitudes, he was moved with compassion on them, because they fainted, and were scattered abroad, as sheep having no shepherd.
[Eng.37]	Then saith he unto his disciples, The harvest truly is plenteous, but the labourers are few;
[Eng.38]	Pray ye therefore the Lord of the harvest, that he will send forth labourers into his harvest.
[Eng.1]	And when he had called unto him his twelve disciples, he gave them power against unclean spirits, to cast them out, and to heal all manner of sickness and all manner of disease.
[Eng.2]	Now the names of the twelve apostles are these; The first, Simon, who is called Peter, and Andrew his brother; James the son of Zebedee, and John his brother;
[Eng.3]	Philip, and Bartholomew; Thomas, and Matthew the publican; James the son of Alphaeus, and Lebbaeus, whose surname was Thaddaeus;
[Eng.4]	Simon the Canaanite, and Judas Iscariot, who also betrayed him.
[Eng.5]	These twelve Jesus sent forth, and commanded them, saying, Go not into the way of the Gentiles, and into any city of the Samaritans enter ye not:
[Eng.6]	But go rather to the lost sheep of the house of Israel.
[Eng.7]	And as ye go, preach, saying, The kingdom of heaven is at hand.
[Eng.8]	Heal the sick, cleanse the lepers, raise the dead, cast out devils: freely ye have received, freely give.
[Eng.9]	Provide neither gold, nor silver, nor brass in your purses,
[Eng.10]	Nor scrip for your journey, neither two coats, neither shoes, nor yet staves: for the workman is worthy of his meat.
[Eng.11]	And into whatsoever city or town ye shall enter, enquire who in it is worthy; and there abide till ye go thence.
[Eng.12]	And when ye come into an house, salute it.
[Eng.13]	And if the house be worthy, let your peace come upon it: but if it be not worthy, let your peace return to you.
[Eng.14]	And whosoever shall not receive you, nor hear your words, when ye depart out of that house or city, shake off the dust of your feet.
[Eng.15]	Verily I say unto you, It shall be more tolerable for the land of Sodom and Gomorrha in the day of judgment, than for that city.
[Eng.16]	Behold, I send you forth as sheep in the midst of wolves: be ye therefore wise as serpents, and harmless as doves.
[Eng.17]	But beware of men: for they will deliver you up to the councils, and they will scourge you in their synagogues;
[Eng.18]	And ye shall be brought before governors and kings for my sake, for a testimony against them and the Gentiles.
[Eng.19]	But when they deliver you up, take no thought how or what ye shall speak: for it shall be given you in that same hour what ye shall speak.
[Eng.20]	For it is not ye that speak, but the Spirit of your Father which speaketh in you.
[Eng.21]	And the brother shall deliver up the brother to death, and the father the child: and the children shall rise up against their parents, and cause them to be put to death.
[Eng.22]	And ye shall be hated of all men for my name's sake: but he that endureth to the end shall be saved.
[Eng.23]	But when they persecute you in this city, flee ye into another: for verily I say unto you, Ye shall not have gone over the cities of Israel, till the Son of man be come.
[Eng.24]	The disciple is not above his master, nor the servant above his lord.
[Eng.25]	It is enough for the disciple that he be as his master, and the servant as his lord. If they have called the master of the house Beelzebub, how much more shall they call them of his household?
[Eng.26]	Fear them not therefore: for there is nothing covered, that shall not be revealed; and hid, that shall not be known.
[Eng.27]	What I tell you in darkness, that speak ye in light: and what ye hear in the ear, that preach ye upon the housetops.
[Eng.28]	And fear not them which kill the body, but are not able to kill the soul: but rather fear him which is able to destroy both soul and body in hell.
[Eng.29]	Are not two sparrows sold for a farthing? and one of them shall not fall on the ground without your Father.
[Eng.30]	But the very hairs of your head are all numbered.
[Eng.31]	Fear ye not therefore, ye are of more value than many sparrows.
[Eng.32]	Whosoever therefore shall confess me before men, him will I confess also before my Father which is in heaven.
[Eng.33]	But whosoever shall deny me before men, him will I also deny before my Father which is in heaven.
[Eng.34]	Think not that I am come to send peace on earth: I came not to send peace, but a sword.
[Eng.35]	For I am come to set a man at variance against his father, and the daughter against her mother, and the daughter in law against her mother in law.
[Eng.36]	And a man's foes shall be they of his own household.
[Eng.37]	He that loveth father or mother more than me is not worthy of me: and he that loveth son or daughter more than me is not worthy of me.
[Eng.38]	And he that taketh not his cross, and followeth after me, is not worthy of me.
[Eng.39]	He that findeth his life shall lose it: and he that loseth his life for my sake shall find it.
[Eng.40]	He that receiveth you receiveth me, and he that receiveth me receiveth him that sent me.
[Eng.41]	He that receiveth a prophet in the name of a prophet shall receive a prophet's reward; and he that receiveth a righteous man in the name of a righteous man shall receive a righteous man's reward.
[Eng.42]	And whosoever shall give to drink unto one of these little ones a cup of cold water only in the name of a disciple, verily I say unto you, he shall in no wise lose his reward.
[Eng.1]	And it came to pass, when Jesus had made an end of commanding his twelve disciples, he departed thence to teach and to preach in their cities.
[Eng.2]	Now when John had heard in the prison the works of Christ, he sent two of his disciples,
[Eng.3]	And said unto him, Art thou he that should come, or do we look for another?
[Eng.4]	Jesus answered and said unto them, Go and shew John again those things which ye do hear and see:
[Eng.5]	The blind receive their sight, and the lame walk, the lepers are cleansed, and the deaf hear, the dead are raised up, and the poor have the gospel preached to them.
[Eng.6]	And blessed is he, whosoever shall not be offended in me.
[Eng.7]	And as they departed, Jesus began to say unto the multitudes concerning John, What went ye out into the wilderness to see? A reed shaken with the wind?
[Eng.8]	But what went ye out for to see? A man clothed in soft raiment? behold, they that wear soft clothing are in kings' houses.
[Eng.9]	But what went ye out for to see? A prophet? yea, I say unto you, and more than a prophet.
[Eng.10]	For this is he, of whom it is written, Behold, I send my messenger before thy face, which shall prepare thy way before thee.
[Eng.11]	Verily I say unto you, Among them that are born of women there hath not risen a greater than John the Baptist: notwithstanding he that is least in the kingdom of heaven is greater than he.
[Eng.12]	And from the days of John the Baptist until now the kingdom of heaven suffereth violence, and the violent take it by force.
[Eng.13]	For all the prophets and the law prophesied until John.
[Eng.14]	And if ye will receive it, this is Elias, which was for to come.
[Eng.15]	He that hath ears to hear, let him hear.
[Eng.16]	But whereunto shall I liken this generation? It is like unto children sitting in the markets, and calling unto their fellows,
[Eng.17]	And saying, We have piped unto you, and ye have not danced; we have mourned unto you, and ye have not lamented.
[Eng.18]	For John came neither eating nor drinking, and they say, He hath a devil.
[Eng.19]	The Son of man came eating and drinking, and they say, Behold a man gluttonous, and a winebibber, a friend of publicans and sinners. But wisdom is justified of her children.
[Eng.20]	Then began he to upbraid the cities wherein most of his mighty works were done, because they repented not:
[Eng.21]	Woe unto thee, Chorazin! woe unto thee, Bethsaida! for if the mighty works, which were done in you, had been done in Tyre and Sidon, they would have repented long ago in sackcloth and ashes.
[Eng.22]	But I say unto you, It shall be more tolerable for Tyre and Sidon at the day of judgment, than for you.
[Eng.23]	And thou, Capernaum, which art exalted unto heaven, shalt be brought down to hell: for if the mighty works, which have been done in thee, had been done in Sodom, it would have remained until this day.
[Eng.24]	But I say unto you, That it shall be more tolerable for the land of Sodom in the day of judgment, than for thee.
[Eng.25]	At that time Jesus answered and said, I thank thee, O Father, Lord of heaven and earth, because thou hast hid these things from the wise and prudent, and hast revealed them unto babes.
[Eng.26]	Even so, Father: for so it seemed good in thy sight.
[Eng.27]	All things are delivered unto me of my Father: and no man knoweth the Son, but the Father; neither knoweth any man the Father, save the Son, and he to whomsoever the Son will reveal him.
[Eng.28]	Come unto me, all ye that labour and are heavy laden, and I will give you rest.
[Eng.29]	Take my yoke upon you, and learn of me; for I am meek and lowly in heart: and ye shall find rest unto your souls.
[Eng.30]	For my yoke is easy, and my burden is light.
[Eng.1]	At that time Jesus went on the sabbath day through the corn; and his disciples were an hungred, and began to pluck the ears of corn and to eat.
[Eng.2]	But when the Pharisees saw it, they said unto him, Behold, thy disciples do that which is not lawful to do upon the sabbath day.
[Eng.3]	But he said unto them, Have ye not read what David did, when he was an hungred, and they that were with him;
[Eng.4]	How he entered into the house of God, and did eat the shewbread, which was not lawful for him to eat, neither for them which were with him, but only for the priests?
[Eng.5]	Or have ye not read in the law, how that on the sabbath days the priests in the temple profane the sabbath, and are blameless?
[Eng.6]	But I say unto you, That in this place is one greater than the temple.
[Eng.7]	But if ye had known what this meaneth, I will have mercy, and not sacrifice, ye would not have condemned the guiltless.
[Eng.8]	For the Son of man is Lord even of the sabbath day.
[Eng.9]	And when he was departed thence, he went into their synagogue:
[Eng.10]	And, behold, there was a man which had his hand withered. And they asked him, saying, Is it lawful to heal on the sabbath days? that they might accuse him.
[Eng.11]	And he said unto them, What man shall there be among you, that shall have one sheep, and if it fall into a pit on the sabbath day, will he not lay hold on it, and lift it out?
[Eng.12]	How much then is a man better than a sheep? Wherefore it is lawful to do well on the sabbath days.
[Eng.13]	Then saith he to the man, Stretch forth thine hand. And he stretched it forth; and it was restored whole, like as the other.
[Eng.14]	Then the Pharisees went out, and held a council against him, how they might destroy him.
[Eng.15]	But when Jesus knew it, he withdrew himself from thence: and great multitudes followed him, and he healed them all;
[Eng.16]	And charged them that they should not make him known:
[Eng.17]	That it might be fulfilled which was spoken by Esaias the prophet, saying,
[Eng.18]	Behold my servant, whom I have chosen; my beloved, in whom my soul is well pleased: I will put my spirit upon him, and he shall shew judgment to the Gentiles.
[Eng.19]	He shall not strive, nor cry; neither shall any man hear his voice in the streets.
[Eng.20]	A bruised reed shall he not break, and smoking flax shall he not quench, till he send forth judgment unto victory.
[Eng.21]	And in his name shall the Gentiles trust.
[Eng.22]	Then was brought unto him one possessed with a devil, blind, and dumb: and he healed him, insomuch that the blind and dumb both spake and saw.
[Eng.23]	And all the people were amazed, and said, Is not this the son of David?
[Eng.24]	But when the Pharisees heard it, they said, This fellow doth not cast out devils, but by Beelzebub the prince of the devils.
[Eng.25]	And Jesus knew their thoughts, and said unto them, Every kingdom divided against itself is brought to desolation; and every city or house divided against itself shall not stand:
[Eng.26]	And if Satan cast out Satan, he is divided against himself; how shall then his kingdom stand?
[Eng.27]	And if I by Beelzebub cast out devils, by whom do your children cast them out? therefore they shall be your judges.
[Eng.28]	But if I cast out devils by the Spirit of God, then the kingdom of God is come unto you.
[Eng.29]	Or else how can one enter into a strong man's house, and spoil his goods, except he first bind the strong man? and then he will spoil his house.
[Eng.30]	He that is not with me is against me; and he that gathereth not with me scattereth abroad.
[Eng.31]	Wherefore I say unto you, All manner of sin and blasphemy shall be forgiven unto men: but the blasphemy against the Holy Ghost shall not be forgiven unto men.
[Eng.32]	And whosoever speaketh a word against the Son of man, it shall be forgiven him: but whosoever speaketh against the Holy Ghost, it shall not be forgiven him, neither in this world, neither in the world to come.
[Eng.33]	Either make the tree good, and his fruit good; or else make the tree corrupt, and his fruit corrupt: for the tree is known by his fruit.
[Eng.34]	O generation of vipers, how can ye, being evil, speak good things? for out of the abundance of the heart the mouth speaketh.
[Eng.35]	A good man out of the good treasure of the heart bringeth forth good things: and an evil man out of the evil treasure bringeth forth evil things.
[Eng.36]	But I say unto you, That every idle word that men shall speak, they shall give account thereof in the day of judgment.
[Eng.37]	For by thy words thou shalt be justified, and by thy words thou shalt be condemned.
[Eng.38]	Then certain of the scribes and of the Pharisees answered, saying, Master, we would see a sign from thee.
[Eng.39]	But he answered and said unto them, An evil and adulterous generation seeketh after a sign; and there shall no sign be given to it, but the sign of the prophet Jonas:
[Eng.40]	For as Jonas was three days and three nights in the whale's belly; so shall the Son of man be three days and three nights in the heart of the earth.
[Eng.41]	The men of Nineveh shall rise in judgment with this generation, and shall condemn it: because they repented at the preaching of Jonas; and, behold, a greater than Jonas is here.
[Eng.42]	The queen of the south shall rise up in the judgment with this generation, and shall condemn it: for she came from the uttermost parts of the earth to hear the wisdom of Solomon; and, behold, a greater than Solomon is here.
[Eng.43]	When the unclean spirit is gone out of a man, he walketh through dry places, seeking rest, and findeth none.
[Eng.44]	Then he saith, I will return into my house from whence I came out; and when he is come, he findeth it empty, swept, and garnished.
[Eng.45]	Then goeth he, and taketh with himself seven other spirits more wicked than himself, and they enter in and dwell there: and the last state of that man is worse than the first. Even so shall it be also unto this wicked generation.
[Eng.46]	While he yet talked to the people, behold, his mother and his brethren stood without, desiring to speak with him.
[Eng.47]	Then one said unto him, Behold, thy mother and thy brethren stand without, desiring to speak with thee.
[Eng.48]	But he answered and said unto him that told him, Who is my mother? and who are my brethren?
[Eng.49]	And he stretched forth his hand toward his disciples, and said, Behold my mother and my brethren!
[Eng.50]	For whosoever shall do the will of my Father which is in heaven, the same is my brother, and sister, and mother.
[Eng.1]	The same day went Jesus out of the house, and sat by the sea side.
[Eng.2]	And great multitudes were gathered together unto him, so that he went into a ship, and sat; and the whole multitude stood on the shore.
[Eng.3]	And he spake many things unto them in parables, saying, Behold, a sower went forth to sow;
[Eng.4]	And when he sowed, some seeds fell by the way side, and the fowls came and devoured them up:
[Eng.5]	Some fell upon stony places, where they had not much earth: and forthwith they sprung up, because they had no deepness of earth:
[Eng.6]	And when the sun was up, they were scorched; and because they had no root, they withered away.
[Eng.7]	And some fell among thorns; and the thorns sprung up, and choked them:
[Eng.8]	But other fell into good ground, and brought forth fruit, some an hundredfold, some sixtyfold, some thirtyfold.
[Eng.9]	Who hath ears to hear, let him hear.
[Eng.10]	And the disciples came, and said unto him, Why speakest thou unto them in parables?
[Eng.11]	He answered and said unto them, Because it is given unto you to know the mysteries of the kingdom of heaven, but to them it is not given.
